## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: constitutive modeling of materials
**Analysis**: This task aims to discover a constitutive equation for stress (sigma) as a function of strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), a central problem in solid mechanics and materials science. Physically, stress typically increases with strain due to work hardening and decreases with temperature due to thermal softening, often through a separable product of strain and temperature functions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic, no temperature effect)
- Linear thermal-elastic: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T (stress from total strain including thermal expansion)
- Linear softening modulus: sigma = (c0 - c1 * T) * epsilon (temperature-dependent elastic modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (parabolic hardening, constant temperature)
- Power-law with linear thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T)
- Power-law with exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (c2 < 0 for softening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturating hardening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal factor: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - (c3 * (T - c4))**c5) (thermal softening with reference temperature)
- Arrhenius-activated flow stress: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (stress decreases with increasing T)
- Exponential hardening: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * epsilon) (large strain behavior, e.g., rubber elasticity)
- Bilinear hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * max(0, epsilon - c2) (elastic-plastic with linear hardening)
- Polynomial hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2 (yield plus parabolic hardening)
- Sigmoidal thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) / (1 + exp(c3 * (T - c4))) (glass transition or phase change effect)
- Hyperbolic tangent saturation: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * (1 - c2 * T) (saturating hardening with linear softening)
- Creep-like power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law dependence on both strain and temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Stress increases monotonically with strain → use power, exponential, polynomial, or saturating forms like (1 - exp(-c*epsilon))
- Thermal softening reduces flow stress → include factors like (1 - c*T), exp(-c*T), or exp(c/T) with positive c
- Linear elasticity at small strains → model must contain a linear term c0*epsilon (often dominant at low strain)
- Plastic yield and hardening → additive constant c0 (yield stress) plus strain-dependent term
- Saturation at large strains → exponential decay to an asymptote: c0 * (1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)) or rational epsilon/(c+epsilon)
- Separability of strain and temperature effects → product of a strain function and a temperature function: f(epsilon) * g(T)
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation → flow stress scales with exp(constant / T), reflecting thermally activated dislocation motion
- Temperature-dependent modulus → elastic term multiplied by (1 - c*T) or exp(-c*T) to capture modulus decrease with heating
- Temperature appears in a ratio such as (T - T_ref)/(T_melt - T_ref) → consider generic normalized temperature forms like (c1 * T + c2)**c3
- For monotonic loading and no strain rate effects, all models are monotonic and smooth; avoid oscillatory or periodic structures

Setting c3=1, c4=0: `T*sin(epsilon)` and `sin(epsilon)` ✓. But it has `T*epsilon**2` instead of `T*epsilon`, and `epsilon**2` instead of `epsilon`, and no `epsilon**3`. **NO MATCH.**

Has `T*epsilon` ✓, but `sqrt(T)*epsilon**4` ≠ `epsilon**3`, and `exp(c6*epsilon)*sin(...)` can't give `T*sin(epsilon)`. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 56:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon**c2*sqrt(T*c3) + c4*epsilon + c5*epsilon**c2 + c6*exp(c7*epsilon)*sin(c8 + c9*epsilon)`

Has `T*epsilon`, `sqrt(T)*epsilon**c2`, `epsilon**c2`, `exp(...)*sin(...)`. The `sqrt(T)` term can't produce `T*sin(epsilon)`. **NO MATCH.**
